<strong>Solution:</strong> No, for various reasons. Intuitively, a subsequence is a sequence that can be derived from another sequence by removing some or no elements without chaning the order of the remaining elements. This obviously is not the case for the two given sequences.<br>
More formally, a subsequence of <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span so in particular <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math><semantics><mrow><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><msub><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi></msub><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>U</mi><mi>l</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">UlUlUl​UlU_lUl​UlUl​Ul​</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.84444em; <li>If <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math><semantics><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><msub><mo>}</mo><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="double-struck">N</mi></mrow></mrow></msub><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">snn∈N{sn}n∈Nsn​n∈N​{sn}n∈N\{ s_n\}_{n \in \mathbb{N}}{sn​}n∈N​snn∈N{sn​}n∈N​sn​n∈N​</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathit" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span><span class="mord">​</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathit">s</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span></span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathit mtight">n</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span class=""></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">}</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.332223em;"><span class="" style="top: -2.55em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathit" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span><span class="mord">​</span><span class="mord mathit">s</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.72243em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathit" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathit">s</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mord">​</span></span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.72243em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathit" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span><span class="mord">​</span><span class="mord mathit">s</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mord">​</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.68333em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathit" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span><span class="mord">​</span></span></span></span></span> is a sequence of real numbers with limit <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math><semantics><mrow><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">LLLLLLLLL</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.68333em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span></span></span></span></span>, prove that this limit is unique.<br>
<strong>Solution:</strong> First, if a sequence has a limit it is by definition convergent. So the statement to prove can be restated as "For all convergent sequences there exists a unique limit <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math><semantics><mrow><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi><mi>L</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">LLLLLLLLL</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.68333em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span><span class="mord mathit">L</span></span></span></span></span>". We’re going to prove this by contradiction, assuming that there exists one convergent sequence which does not have a unique limit.<br>
Let <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math><semantics><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><msub><mo>}</mo><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="double-struck">N</mi></mrow></mrow></msub><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mrow><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi></mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">​</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">snn∈N{sn}n∈Nsn​n∈N​{sn}n∈N\{ s_n\}_{n \in \mathbb{N}}{sn​}n∈N​snn∈N{sn​}n∈N​sn​n∈N​</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathit">s</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mord mathit">n</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" encoding="application/x-tex">∣l1−l2∣=∣l1−am0+am0+l2∣≤∣l1−am0∣+∣am0−l2∣&lt;ϵ+ϵ=2ϵ=23∣l1−l2∣.∣l1−l2∣=∣l1−am0+am0+l2∣≤∣l1−am0∣+∣am0−l2∣&lt;ϵ+ϵ=2ϵ=23∣l1−l2∣.∣l1​−l2​∣​=∣l1​−am0​​+am0​​+l2​∣≤∣l1​−am0​​∣+∣am0​​−l2​∣&lt;ϵ+ϵ=2ϵ=32​∣l1​−l2​∣.​∣l1−l2∣=∣l1−am0+am0+l2∣≤∣l1−am0∣+∣am0−l2∣&lt;ϵ+ϵ=2ϵ=23∣l1−l2∣.
\begin{aligned}
|l_1 - l_2| &amp;= |l_1 - a_{m_0}  + a_{m_0} + l_2| \\
&amp;\leq |l_1 - a_{m_0}| + |a_{m_0} - l_2| \\
&amp;&lt; \epsilon + \epsilon \\
&amp;= 2\epsilon = \frac{2}{3}|l_1 - l_2|.
\end{aligned}
